CentralNotice -->\n   </div>\n   <div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n   </div>\n   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">\n    US Orbital Segment\n   </h1>\n   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">\n     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia\n    </div>\n    <div id="contentSub">\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n     Jump to:\n     <a href="#mw-head">\n      navigation\n     </a>\n     ,\n     <a href="#p-search">\n      search\n     </a>\n    </div>\n    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">\n     <div class="mw-parser-output">\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       "USOS" redirects here. For the professional wrestling tag team, see\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Usos" title="The Usos">\n        The Usos\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Orbital_Segment_-_May_2011.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3368" data-file-width="2256" height="448" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/US_Orbital_Segment_-_May_2011.jpg/300px-US_Orbital_Segment_-_May_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/US_Orbital_Segment_-_May_2011.jpg/450px-US_Orbital_Segment_-_May_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/US_Orbital_Segment_-_May_2011.jpg/600px-US_Orbital_Segment_-_May_2011.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Orbital_Segment_-_May_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The US Orbital Segment with\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n          Space Shuttle\n         </a>\n         docked. Zarya is also a NASA module but it is Russian-made\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        US Orbital Segment\n       </b>\n       (\n       <b>\n        USOS\n       </b>\n       ) is the name given to the components of the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS) constructed and operated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        National Aeronautics and Space Administration\n       </a>\n       (NASA),\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        European Space Agency\n       </a>\n       (ESA),\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">\n        Canadian Space Agency\n       </a>\n       (CSA) and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_Aerospace_Exploration_Agency" title="Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency">\n        Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency\n       </a>\n       (JAXA). The segment currently consists of eleven pressurized components and various external elements, all of which were delivered by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The segment is monitored and controlled from various mission control centers on the world including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">\n        Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" title="Houston, Texas">\n        Houston, Texas\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Control_Center" title="Columbus Control Center">\n        Columbus Control Center\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Oberpfaffenhofen" title="Oberpfaffenhofen">\n        Oberpfaffenhofen\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">\n        Germany\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Tsukuba_Space_Center" title="Tsukuba Space Center">\n        Tsukuba Space Center\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsukuba" title="Tsukuba">\n        Tsukuba\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">\n        Japan\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">\n        Marshall Space Flight Center\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">\n        Huntsville, Alabama\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li href="#Destiny">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               1.2.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Destiny\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-8">\n             <a href="#Columbus">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               1.2.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Columbus\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-9">\n             <a href="#Kibo">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               1.2.3\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Kibo\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n           <a href="#Other_Modules">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Other Modules\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-11">\n             <a href="#Quest">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               1.3.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Quest\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-12">\n             <a href="#Leonardo">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               1.3.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Leonardo\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13">\n             <a Adapter\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14">\n         <a    <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15">\n           <a href="#Integrated_Truss_Structure">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Integrated Truss Structure\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16">\n           <a          </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             ExPRESS logistics carrier\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer_2">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer 2\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Mobile_Servicing_System">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Mobile Servicing System\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-20">\n             <a href="#Canadarm2">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.5.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Canadarm2\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-21">\n             <a href="#Special_Purpose_Dextrous_Manipulator">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.5.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Special Purpose Dextrous Manipulator\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-22">\n             <a href="#Mobile_Base_System">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.5.3\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Mobile Base System\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-23">\n             <a href="#Enhanced_ISS_Boom_Assembly">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               2.5.4\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Enhanced ISS Boom Assembly\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24">\n         <a <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Modules">\n        Modules\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Modules">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_configuration_2011-05_en.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1257" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/ISS_configuration_2011-05_en.svg/300px-ISS_configuration_2011-05_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/ISS_configuration_2011-05_en.svg/450px-ISS_configuration_2011-05_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/ISS_configuration_2011-05_en.svg/600px-ISS_configuration_2011-05_en.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS_configuration_2011-05_en.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         ISS configuration as of May 2011.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The US Orbital Segment consists of 11 pressurized modules. Of these, eight are habitable, and three are connecting nodes with large ports. The ports are used to connect the modules together or provide berths and docks for spacecraft.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Nodes">\n        Nodes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Nodes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Each of the nodes has ports called\n       <a href="/wiki/Common_Berthing_Mechanism" title="Common Berthing Mechanism">\n        Common Berthing Mechanisms\n       </a>\n       (CBM). All three nodes have 4 ports around their exterior, and 1 port on each end, 6 ports in total. In addition to the 18 ports on the nodes there are additional ports on the modules, most of these are used for mating modules together, while unused CBM ports can berth one of the re-supply spacecraft MPLM, HTV, Dragon Cargo or Cygnus. There are two\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressurized_Mating_Adapter" title="Pressurized Mating Adapter">\n        PMA\n       </a>\n       adapters that change CBM ports to\n       <a href="/wiki/Androgynous_Peripheral_Attach_System#APAS-95" title="Androgynous Peripheral Attach System">\n        docking ports\n       </a>\n       , the type used by Soyuz, Progress and Automated Transfer Vehicle spacecraft, this is the same port the former Space Shuttle used. It\'s a flexible system where the layout is changed as needed.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Unity">\n        Unity\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Unity">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The first component of the USOS pressurized segment is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Unity_(ISS_module)" title="Unity (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Unity node\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       . On the aft end of\n       <i>\n        Unity\n       </i>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressurized_Mating_Adapter" title="Pressurized Mating Adapter">\n        Pressurized Mating Adapter\n       </a>\n       (PMA) 1. The PMA-1 connects\n       <i>\n        Unity\n       </i>\n       with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orbital_Segment" title="Russian Orbital Segment">\n        Russian segment\n       </a>\n       . Unity is also connected to the Quest airlock on the starboard side,\n       <i>\n        Tranquility\n       </i>\n       on the port side, and the Z1 truss on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Zenith" title="Zenith">\n        zenith\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       lab connects to the forward end, leading to the rest of the USOS.\n       <i>\n        Unity\n       </i>\n       is also used by the crews on board the ISS to eat meals and share some downtime together. The\n       <i>\n        Unity\n       </i>\n       node was delivered to the station by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-88" title="STS-88">\n        STS-88\n       </a>\n       on December 6, 1998.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts88_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts88-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Harmony">\n        Harmony\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Harmony">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Harmony_(ISS_module)" title="Harmony (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Harmony node\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       is the central connecting node of the USOS.\n       <i>\n        Harmony\n       </i>\n       connects to the\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       lab aft end,\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       lab to the port side, and\n       <i>\n        Columbus\n       </i>\n       lab to the starboard side. The\n       <i>\n        Harmony\n       </i>\n       node\'s nadir and zenith ports also serves as the berthing port for\n       <a href="/wiki/H-II_Transfer_Vehicle" title="H-II Transfer Vehicle">\n        H-II Transfer Vehicle\n       </a>\n       (HTV),\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n        Dragon\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_(spacecraft)" title="Cygnus (spacecraft)">\n        Cygnus\n       </a>\n       resupply vehicles. On the forward end of\n       <i>\n        Harmony\n       </i>\n       is PMA-2, which was used by visiting\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttles\n       </a>\n       as a mating adapter and by future manned missions to the ISS.\n       <i>\n        Harmony\n       </i>\n       was delivered by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-120" title="STS-120">\n        STS-120\n       </a>\n       mission on October 23, 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts120_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts120-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tranquility_and_Cupola">\n        Tranquility and Cupola\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tranquility and Cupola">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Tranquility_(ISS_module)" title="Tranquility (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Tranquility node\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       houses the USOS life support systems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-node3_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-node3-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Tranquility\n       </i>\n       also hosts the seven windowed\n       <a href="/wiki/Cupola_(ISS_module)" title="Cupola (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Cupola\n        </i>\n        module\n       </a>\n       and the Leonardo modile on its forward port. The\n       <i>\n        Cupola\n       </i>\n       is used for Earth observation and robotic operations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cupola_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cupola-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The forward facing port of\n       <i>\n        Tranquility\n       </i>\n       is blocked by the station\'s truss structure, while the aft facing port is free for use. While the nadir port is used by the\n       <i>\n        Cupola\n       </i>\n       , the zenith port is used by some exercise equipment inside the node. The port side port is occupied by the PMA 3, and the starboard port is connected to node 1. The\n       <i>\n        Cupola\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        Tranquility\n       </i>\n       modules were delivered by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-130" title="STS-130">\n        STS-130\n       </a>\n       in February 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts130_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts130-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Laboratories">\n        Laboratories\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Laboratories">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Destiny">\n        Destiny\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Destiny">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Destiny_(ISS_module)" title="Destiny (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Destiny laboratory\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       is the American-built laboratory module. It is used for medical, engineering, biotechnological, physics, materials science and Earth science research.\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       also houses a back-up robotic work station, and was the first of the USOS laboratories to be delivered. It was delivered by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-98" title="STS-98">\n        STS-98\n       </a>\n       on February 7, 2001.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts98_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts98-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       lab is managed by mission control centers in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" title="Houston, Texas">\n        Houston\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">\n        Texas\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">\n        Huntsville\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">\n        Alabama\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Columbus">\n        Columbus\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Columbus">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbus_(ISS_module)" title="Columbus (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Columbus\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       is a laboratory module built by the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        European Space Agency\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa1_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-esa1-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is host to scientific research in fluids, biology, medicine, materials and Earth sciences.\n       <i>\n        Columbus\n       </i>\n       also has four external payload locations, used to expose experiments to the vacuum of space. The\n       <i>\n        Columbus\n       </i>\n       module was delivered to the ISS by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-122" title="STS-122">\n        STS-122\n       </a>\n       on February 7, 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts122_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts122-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Control_Center" title="Columbus Control Center">\n        Columbus Control Center\n       </a>\n       , located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">\n        Germany\n       </a>\n       , is responsible for the\n       <i>\n        Columbus\n       </i>\n       module.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kibo">\n        Kibo\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Kibo">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USOS_window_identification.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="688" data-file-width="1043" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/USOS_window_identification.png/220px-USOS_window_identification.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/USOS_window_identification.png/330px-USOS_window_identification.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/USOS_window_identification.png/440px-USOS_window_identification.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USOS_window_identification.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         USOS International Space Station window locations\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Kibo_(ISS_module)" title="Kibo (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Kibo laboratory\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       is the Japanese component of the USOS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jaxa1_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-jaxa1-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       has four main parts: the\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       lab itself, a pressurized cargo container, an exposed science platform and two robotic arms. The module is unique in that it has a small airlock, which can be used to pass payloads to the robotic arms or astronauts outside the station. The robotic arms are controlled from a work station inside the lab. The lab is used for research in medicine, engineering, biotechnology, physics, materials science and Earth science. The logistics container was the first part of\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       to arrive. It was delivered by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-123" title="STS-123">\n        STS-123\n       </a>\n       in March 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts123_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts123-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       lab itself was delivered to the ISS by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-124" title="STS-124">\n        STS-124\n       </a>\n       mission in May 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts124_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts124-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The exposed facility was brought to the ISS by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-127" title="STS-127">\n        STS-127\n       </a>\n       mission in July 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts127_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts127-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The JEM Control center in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsukuba,_Japan" title="Tsukuba, Japan">\n        Tsukuba, Japan\n       </a>\n       is responsible for all elements of the\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       laboratory.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_Modules">\n        Other Modules\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Other Modules">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Quest">\n        Quest\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Quest">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_Quest_airlock.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1904" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/ISS_Quest_airlock.jpg/220px-ISS_Quest_airlock.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/ISS_Quest_airlock.jpg/330px-ISS_Quest_airlock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/ISS_Quest_airlock.jpg/440px-ISS_Quest_airlock.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS_Quest_airlock.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <center>\n          Quest\n         </center>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Quest_Joint_Airlock" title="Quest Joint Airlock">\n        <i>\n         Quest\n        </i>\n        Joint Airlock\n       </a>\n       is used to host spacewalks from the USOS segment of the ISS. It consists of two main parts: the equipment lock and the crew lock. The equipment lock is where the\n       <a href="/wiki/Extravehicular_Mobility_Unit" title="Extravehicular Mobility Unit">\n        Extravehicular Mobility Units\n       </a>\n       are stored and preparations for spacewalks are carried out. The crew lock is depressurized during spacewalks. The\n       <i>\n        Quest\n       </i>\n       airlock was delivered and installed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-104" title="STS-104">\n        STS-104\n       </a>\n       crew in July 2001.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts104_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts104-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Leonardo">\n        Leonardo\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Leonardo">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       module, also known as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Permanent_Multipurpose_Module" title="Permanent Multipurpose Module">\n        Permanent Multipurpose Module\n       </a>\n       (PMM), is a module used for stowage space on the ISS.\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       is attached to the forward-facing side of the\n       <i>\n        Tranquility\n       </i>\n       node. The PMM was delivered to the ISS by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-133" title="STS-133">\n        STS-133\n       </a>\n       mission in early 2011. Originally the\n       <a href="/wiki/Multi-Purpose_Logistics_Module" title="Multi-Purpose Logistics Module">\n        Multi-Purpose Logistics Module\n       </a>\n       (MPLM)\n       <i>\n        Leonardo\n       </i>\n       , it was converted to stay on orbit for an extended period of time prior to being installed on the ISS.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pressurized_Mating_Adapter">\n        Pressurized Mating Adapter\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Pressurized Mating Adapter">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressurized_Mating_Adapter" title="Pressurized Mating Adapter">\n        Pressurized Mating Adapters\n       </a>\n       (PMA) serve as docking ports on the USOS portion of the ISS. Currently PMA-1 is used to connect the\n       <i>\n        Unity\n       </i>\n       node with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zarya_(ISS_module)" title="Zarya (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Zarya\n        </i>\n        module\n       </a>\n       on the ISS. Pressurized Mating Adapter-2 is located on the forward end of\n       <i>\n        Harmony\n       </i>\n       , and was used by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       to dock with the ISS. Any future manned American spaceflights to the ISS will use PMA-2. The third Pressurized Mating Adapter is located on the aft end of the\n       <i>\n        Tranquility\n       </i>\n       node. Currently, PMA-3 serves only as a storage location, and serves as a back up to PMA-2. PMA-1 and PMA-2 were delivered with the\n       <i>\n        Unity\n       </i>\n       node on STS-88 in December 1998.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts88_1-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts88-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The third PMA was delivered by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-92" title="STS-92">\n        STS-92\n       </a>\n       on October 11, 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts92_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts92-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="External_elements">\n        External elements\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: External elements">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Integrated_Truss_Structure">\n        Integrated Truss Structure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Integrated Truss Structure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:304px;max-width:304px">\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_Truss_structure.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/ISS_Truss_structure.jpg/300px-ISS_Truss_structure.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/ISS_Truss_structure.jpg/450px-ISS_Truss_structure.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/ISS_Truss_structure.jpg/600px-ISS_Truss_structure.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Image taken during\n          <a href="/wiki/STS-113" title="STS-113">\n           STS-113\n          </a>\n          in 2002 showing a portion of the ITS.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:302px;max-width:302px">\n         <div class="thumbimage">\n          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:S122e008269.jpg">\n           <img alt="" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3032" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/S122e008269.jpg/300px-S122e008269.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/S122e008269.jpg/450px-S122e008269.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/S122e008269.jpg/600px-S122e008269.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">\n          Image taken during\n          <a href="/wiki/STS-122" title="STS-122">\n           STS-122\n          </a>\n          in 2008 showing an ITS segment with solar array attached at one end.\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n        Integrated Truss Structure\n       </a>\n       (ITS) houses vital equipment on the exterior of the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-its_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-its-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Each segment of truss is given a designation of P or S, indicating whether the segment is on the port or starboard side, and a number which indicates its position on its respective side. The truss system itself consists of 12 total segments\xe2\x80\x94four on each side, and one central segment\xe2\x80\x94which are connected to the ISS by attachment points on the\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       module.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-its2_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-its2-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The thirteenth piece, known as the Zenith-1 (Z1) truss segment, is attached to the\n       <i>\n        Unity\n       </i>\n       module, and was originally used to hold the P6\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_array" title="Solar array">\n        solar arrays\n       </a>\n       to provide power to the USOS. The Z1 segment now houses the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ku_band" title="Ku band">\n        K\n        <sub>\n         u\n        </sub>\n        -band\n       </a>\n       antennas and serves as a routing point for power and data cables on the exterior of the ISS. The Integrated Truss Structure houses four sets of solar arrays. Each set of solar arrays contains four arrays for a total of 16 solar arrays. Each of the four sets of arrays also has an associated cooling system and radiator for cooling the power supply equipment. The Integrated Truss Structure also houses the main cooling system for the ISS, which consists of two pumps, two radiator arrays, and two ammonia and two nitrogen tank assemblies. There are also several payload attachment points located on the Integrated Truss Structure. These points host the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/External_Stowage_Platform" title="External Stowage Platform">\n        External Stowage Platforms\n       </a>\n       , External Logistics Carriers,\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer" title="Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer">\n        Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer\n       </a>\n       and the Mobile Base System for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2" title="Canadarm2">\n        Canadarm2\n       </a>\n       . The Z1 truss was delivered by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-92" title="STS-92">\n        STS-92\n       </a>\n       mission in October 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts92_14-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts92-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The P6 segment was installed on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-97" title="STS-97">\n        STS-97\n       </a>\n       in December 2000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts97_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts97-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The S0 truss was delivered to the ISS on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-110" title="STS-110">\n        STS-110\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts110_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts110-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with the S1 segment following on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-112" title="STS-112">\n        STS-112\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts112_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts112-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The P1 segment of the truss was brought to the ISS by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-113" title="STS-113">\n        STS-113\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts113_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts113-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       followed by the P3/P4 segment on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-115" title="STS-115">\n        STS-115\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts115_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts115-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the P5 segment on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-116" title="STS-116">\n        STS-116\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts116_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts116-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The S3/S4 truss segment was delivered by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-117" title="STS-117">\n        STS-117\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts117_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts117-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       followed by the S5 segment\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n        STS-118\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts118_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts118-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The last component of the truss segment, the S6 segment, was delivered by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-119" title="STS-119">\n        STS-119\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts119_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts119-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="External_Stowage_Platform">\n        External Stowage Platform\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: External Stowage Platform">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/External_Stowage_Platform" title="External Stowage Platform">\n        External Stowage Platforms\n       </a>\n       (ESP), are a series of platforms that are used to store\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_Replacement_Units" title="Orbital Replacement Units">\n        Orbital Replacement Units\n       </a>\n       (ORU) on the ISS. The ESP\'s provide power to the ORU\'s but do not allow command and data handling. External Stowage Platform 1 is located on the port side of the\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       lab and was delivered on the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-102" title="STS-102">\n        STS-102\n       </a>\n       mission in March 2001.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts102_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts102-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ESP-2 is located on the port side of the\n       <i>\n        Quest\n       </i>\n       airlock, and was brought to the ISS by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-114" title="STS-114">\n        STS-114\n       </a>\n       crew in 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts114_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts114-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ESP-3 is located on the Starboard 3 (S3) truss segment and was delivered to the ISS on the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n        STS-118\n       </a>\n       mission in August 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts118_24-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts118-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="ExPRESS_logistics_carrier">\n        ExPRESS logistics carrier\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: ExPRESS logistics carrier">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ExPRESS_logistics_carrier" title="ExPRESS logistics carrier">\n        ExPRESS logistics carriers\n       </a>\n       (ELCs) are similar to the External Stowage Platform, but designed to carry more cargo. Unlike the ESPs, the ELCs allow for command and data handling. This allows science experiments to be mounted to the ELCs. ExPRESS Logistics Carriers 1, located on the lower P3 truss, and ELC 2, located on the upper S3 truss, were delivered by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-129" title="STS-129">\n        STS-129\n       </a>\n       mission in November 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts129_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts129-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ELC-3 was brought to the ISS by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-134" title="STS-134">\n        STS-134\n       </a>\n       crew, is located on the upper P3 truss.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts134_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts134-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ELC-4 was delivered and installed on the lower S3 truss segment, during the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-133" title="STS-133">\n        STS-133\n       </a>\n       mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts133_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts133-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer_2">\n        Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer 2\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer 2">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer" title="Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer">\n        Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer\n       </a>\n       (AMS) is a particle physics experiment that is mounted on the S3 truss segment. The AMS is designed to search for\n       <a href="/wiki/Dark_matter" title="Dark matter">\n        dark matter\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-matter" title="Anti-matter">\n        anti-matter\n       </a>\n       . Five hundred scientists from 56 different institutions and 16 countries participated in the development and construction of the AMS. The Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer was delivered by the STS-134 crew.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts134_29-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts134-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_Servicing_System">\n        Mobile Servicing System\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mobile Servicing System">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Servicing_System" title="Mobile Servicing System">\n        Mobile Servicing System\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The components of the MSS were supplied by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">\n        Canadian Space Agency\n       </a>\n       in conjunction with\n       <a href="/wiki/MDA_Space_Missions" title="MDA Space Missions">\n        MDA Space Missions\n       </a>\n       . The Mobile Transporter that carries the Mobile Base System was designed and built by Northrop Grumman under contract with NASA.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Canadarm2">\n        Canadarm2\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Canadarm2">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The main component of the mobile servicing system is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2" title="Canadarm2">\n        Canadarm2\n       </a>\n       , also known as the Space Station Remote Manipulator System (SSRMS). The arm is capable of moving large, heavy payloads that cannot be handled by astronauts during a spacewalk. The arm has a payload capacity of 116,000\n       <a href="/wiki/Kilogram" title="Kilogram">\n        kg\n       </a>\n       (256,000\n       <a href="/wiki/Pound_(mass)" title="Pound (mass)">\n        lb\n       </a>\n       ), and 7 degrees of freedom.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mss_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mss-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Canadarm2 is also capable of changing where it is stationed and what end is used. There are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grapple_Fixture" title="Grapple Fixture">\n        grapple fixtures\n       </a>\n       for the Candarm2 on the\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       lab,\n       <i>\n        Harmony\n       </i>\n       node,\n       <i>\n        Unity\n       </i>\n       node and the Mobile Base System. A grapple fixture is installed on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zarya_(ISS_module)" title="Zarya (ISS module)">\n        <i>\n         Zarya\n        </i>\n        module\n       </a>\n       , but does not have data cables connected. Once these cables are connected, the Canadarm2 will be able to position itself on the exterior of\n       <i>\n        Zarya\n       </i>\n       and will be able to support\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_Activity" title="Extra-vehicular Activity">\n        Extra-vehicular Activity\n       </a>\n       (EVA) in the vicinity the Russian Orbital Segment (ROS). The Canadarm2 was assembled and installed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-100" title="STS-100">\n        STS-100\n       </a>\n       crew in early 2001.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts100_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts100-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Special_Purpose_Dextrous_Manipulator">\n        Special Purpose Dextrous Manipulator\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Special Purpose Dextrous Manipulator">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Dextre" title="Dextre">\n        Dextre\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_Purpose_Dexterous_Manipulator" title="Special Purpose Dexterous Manipulator">\n        Special Purpose Dexterous Manipulator\n       </a>\n       (SPDM), also known as\n       <i>\n        Dextre\n       </i>\n       , is a two armed robot that can be attached to the ISS, the Mobile Base System or Canadarm2.\n       <i>\n        Dextre\n       </i>\n       is capable of performing tasks that would otherwise require an astronaut to perform. These tasks include switching\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_replacement_unit" title="Orbital replacement unit">\n        orbital replacement units\n       </a>\n       or moving ORUs from their stowage locations to where they are to be installed. Using\n       <i>\n        Dextre\n       </i>\n       can reduce preparatory time needed to perform certain tasks and afford astronauts the ability to invest more time in the completion of other tasks.\n       <i>\n        Dextre\'\n       </i>\n       s primary grapple fixture is located on the\n       <i>\n        Destiny\n       </i>\n       lab, but can also be mounted on any powered grapple fixture on the ISS. It has a payload capacity of 600\xc2\xa0kg (1,300\xc2\xa0lb), and 15 degrees of freedom.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mss_31-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mss-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <i>\n        Dextre\n       </i>\n       was delivered to the ISS by\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-123" title="STS-123">\n        STS-123\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts123_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts123-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_Base_System">\n        Mobile Base System\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Mobile Base System">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2#Mobile_Base_System" title="Canadarm2">\n        Mobile Base System\n       </a>\n       (MBS) is a rail car-like device installed on the Integrated Truss Structure of the ISS. It weighs 886\n       <a href="/wiki/Kilogram" title="Kilogram">\n        kg\n       </a>\n       (1,953\n       <a href="/wiki/Pound_(mass)" title="Pound (mass)">\n        lb\n       </a>\n       ), and has a payload capacity of 20,954\xc2\xa0kg (46,196\xc2\xa0lb).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mbs1_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mbs1-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The MBS can move from the Starboard 3 (S3) to the Port 3 (P3) truss segments and has a top speed of 2.5\n       <a href="/wiki/Metre_per_second" title="Metre per second">\n        cm/s\n       </a>\n       (0.082\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feet_per_second" title="Feet per second">\n        ft/s\n       </a>\n       ). The MBS has four\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_Data_Grapple_Fixture" title="Power Data Grapple Fixture">\n        PDGFs\n       </a>\n       which can be used as mounts for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2" title="Canadarm2">\n        Canadarm2\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Dextre" title="Dextre">\n        Dextre\n       </a>\n       , as well as a Payload/Orbital Replacement Unit Accommodations (POA), to hold payloads and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_Replacement_Units" title="Orbital Replacement Units">\n        Orbital Replacement Units\n       </a>\n       (ORUs). The MBS also has a common attach system, to grapple a special capture bar on payloads. It also has its own main computer and video distribution units, and remote power control modules.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mbs2_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mbs2-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The MBS was delivered on\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-111" title="STS-111">\n        STS-111\n       </a>\n       in June 2002.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts111_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts111-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Enhanced_ISS_Boom_Assembly">\n        Enhanced ISS Boom Assembly\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Enhanced ISS Boom Assembly">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbiter_Boom_Sensor_System#Enhanced_ISS_Boom_Assembly" title="Orbiter Boom Sensor System">\n        Enhanced ISS Boom Assembly\n       </a>\n       is used to extend the reach of Canadarm2 and provides detailed inspection capability. There are lasers and cameras at the end of the boom able to record at a resolution of a few millimeters. The boom is also fitted with handrails, so that it can assist spacewalkers during EVAs as was done on STS-120 to repair the solar arrays.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/NASA_X-38" title="NASA X-38">\n         NASA X-38\n        </a>\n        , canceled crew return vehicle\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_HL-20" title="NASA HL-20">\n         NASA HL-20\n        </a>\n        /\n        <a href="/wiki/Dream_Chaser" title="Dream Chaser">\n         Dream Chaser\n        </a>\n        proposed crew return vehicle\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orbital_Segment" title="Russian Orbital Segment">\n         Russian Orbital Segment\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=US_Orbital_Segment&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: References">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em;
